## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical kinetics
**Analysis**: This task involves predicting the rate of change of concentration in a chemical reaction, which is a fundamental concept in chemical kinetics. The concentration at time t (A) and time itself (t) are key variables in this analysis.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- First-order rate law: dA/dt = -k * A (monomolecular reaction)
- Second-order rate law: dA/dt = -k * A^2 (bimolecular reaction)
- Zhou-Frank-Kuczynski (ZFK) model: dA/dt = -k * A^m * (A_t - A)^n (modified reaction kinetics with fitting parameters)
- Prout-Tompkins equation: dA/dt = -k1 * A * (k2/A)^1/(k2/A) ( reaction with pre-exponential factor variation)
- Law of mass action: dA/dt = k * A * B (bimolecular reaction between A and B)
- Homogeneous autocatalytic reaction: dA/dt = k * A * (1 - A/A_c) (reaction with saturation term)
- First-order deactivation reaction: dA/dt = k * A * (1 - A/A_0) (reaction with saturation term)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA/dt = k * A * B (reaction with autocatalytic term)
-  Michaelis-Menten kinetics: dA/dt = k * S * A / (A + K) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction kinetics)
- Birth-death process: dA/dt = (birth_rate * A) - (death_rate * A) (random chemical reaction kinetics)
- Pre-exponential factor variation: dA/dt = A * exp(-k * t) (decay process with varying rate)
- First-order reversible reaction: dA/dt = -k1 * A + k2 * B (reversible chemical reaction with two steps)
- Cooperative binding: dA/dt = k * A * B / (1 + k * A * B) (binding reaction with cooperative binding term)
- bimolecular isomerization: dA/dt = k * A^2 (isomerization reaction with no other variables involved)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Pure saturation effect → Logistic equation A/(1+A) (when dA/dt reaches a steady state and concentration approaches A_c)
- Variable rate effect → Rational exponential A/(A+c1) or rational function (when reaction rate varies due to other factors and terms)
- Pure first-order effect → Exponential decay term A*exp(-c*t) (simple decay process without complicating terms)
- Cooperative binding behavior → Power-law fraction A^c/(A^c+c1) (when two or more variables interact to influence the rate of change)
- Growth to saturation → Logistic-like function A/(1+A)^c (general population growth with no decay rate involved)
- Effect of autocatalytic term → Piecewise functions for different ranges of A (describing the emergence of autocatalytic terms at certain thresholds)
- Variable coefficient → Adjusted coefficients for k or B due to environmental factors, which correspond to specific quantitative updates in dA/dt
- Saturating steady-state behavior → Function forms x/(1+x) and logistic curve 1/(1+exp(-c*x))
- Power-law scaling → Cooperative binding (when rate of change changes dramatically at threshold A and affected variables both nonlinearly scale)
- Exponential decay → Rate A * exp(-c*t) leading to growth or saturation forms and stationary decay terms exp(-c*t)
- Burst behavior → A disrupted by noise (A+c1) reflected as fragmented steps resulting in fluctuating behavior, perhaps bursts. Some behaviors (some unrealistic as they strongly diverge to mathematical reality)
